### <a id="inductive-types-h-s-p-and-v">Inductive Types H, S, P, and V</a>

This section presents the [UALib.Varieties.Varieties][] module of the [Agda Universal Algebra Library][].

Fix a signature ğ‘†, let ğ’¦ be a class of ğ‘†-algebras, and define

* H ğ’¦ = algebras isomorphic to a homomorphic image of a members of ğ’¦;
* S ğ’¦ = algebras isomorphic to a subalgebra of a member of ğ’¦;
* P ğ’¦ = algebras isomorphic to a product of members of ğ’¦.

A straight-forward verification confirms that H, S, and P are **closure operators** (expansive, monotone, and idempotent).  A class ğ’¦ of ğ‘†-algebras is said to be *closed under the taking of homomorphic images* provided `H ğ’¦ âŠ† ğ’¦`. Similarly, ğ’¦ is *closed under the taking of subalgebras* (resp., *arbitrary products*) provided `S ğ’¦ âŠ† ğ’¦` (resp., `P ğ’¦ âŠ† ğ’¦`). The operators H, S, and P can be composed with one another repeatedly, forming yet more closure operators.

An algebra is a homomorphic image (resp., subalgebra; resp., product) of every algebra to which it is isomorphic. Thus, the class `H ğ’¦` (resp., `S ğ’¦`; resp., `P ğ’¦`) is closed under isomorphism.

A **variety** is a class of algebras, in the same signature, that is closed under the taking of homomorphic images, subalgebras, and arbitrary products.  To represent varieties we define inductive types for the closure operators `H`, `S`, and `P` that are composable.  Separately, we define an inductive type `V` which simultaneously represents closure under all three operators, `H`, `S`, and `P`.

<pre class="Agda">

#### <a id="homomorphic-closure">Homomorphism closure</a>

We define the inductive type `H` to represent classes of algebras that include all homomorphic images of algebras in the class; i.e., classes that are closed under the taking of homomorphic images.

#### <a id="subalgebra-closure">Subalgebra closure</a>

The most useful inductive type that we have found for representing classes of algebras that are closed under the taking of subalgebras as an inductive type.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="3143" class="Comment">--Closure wrt S</a>
<a id="3159" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="S"></a><a id="3164" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#3164" class="Datatype">S</a> <a id="3166" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="3167" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#3167" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a> <a id="3169" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#3169" class="Bound">ğ“¦</a> <a id="3171" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3173" href="universes.html#551" class="Postulate">Universe</a><a id="3181" class="Symbol">}(</a><a id="3183" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#3183" class="Bound">ğ’¦</a> <a id="3185" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3187" href="UALib.Relations.Unary.html#1082" class="Function">Pred</a> <a id="3192" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="3193" href="UALib.Algebras.Algebras.html#813" class="Function">Algebra</a> <a id="3201" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#3167" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a> <a id="3203" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#1882" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a><a id="3204" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="3206" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="3207" href="UALib.Relations.Congruences.html#933" class="Function">ov</a> <a id="3210" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#3167" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a><a id="3211" class="Symbol">))</a> <a id="3214" class="Symbol">:</a>

<!-- A class ğ’¦ is **closed under** `S` (or `S`-**closed**) provided `S ğ’¦ âŠ† ğ’¦` -->

-----------------------------------------

#### <a id="product-closure">Product closure</a>

The most useful inductive type that we have found for representing classes of algebras closed under arbitrary products is the following.

<pre class="Agda">

<!-- A class ğ’¦ is **closed under** `P` (or `P`-**closed**) provided `P ğ’¦ âŠ† ğ’¦`. -->

-----------------------------------------------

#### <a id="variety-closure">Varietal closure</a>

A class ğ’¦ of ğ‘†-algebras is called a **variety** if it is closed under each of the closure operators H, S, and P introduced above; the corresponding closure operator is often denoted ğ•, but we will typically denote it by `V`.

Thus, if ğ’¦ is a class of ğ‘†-algebras, then the **variety generated by** ğ’¦ is denoted by `V ğ’¦` and defined to be the smallest class that contains ğ’¦ and is closed under `H`, `S`, and `P`.

We now define `V` as an inductive type.

With the closure operator V representing closure under HSP, we formally represent what it means to be a variety of algebras as follows.

-------------------------------

#### <a id="closure-properties">Closure properties</a>

The types defined above represent operators with useful closure properties. We now prove a handful of such properties since we will need them later.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="6677" class="Comment">-- P is a closure operator; in particular, it&#39;s expansive.</a>
<a id="P-expa"></a><a id="6736" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#6736" class="Function">P-expa</a> <a id="6743" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="6745" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="6746" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#6746" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a> <a id="6748" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="6750" href="universes.html#551" class="Postulate">Universe</a><a id="6758" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="6760" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#6760" class="Bound">ğ’¦</a> <a id="6762" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="6764" href="UALib.Relations.Unary.html#1082" class="Function">Pred</a> <a id="6769" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6770" href="UALib.Algebras.Algebras.html#813" class="Function">Algebra</a> <a id="6778" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#6746" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a> <a id="6780" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#1882" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a><a id="6781" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="6783" href="UALib.Relations.Congruences.html#933" class="Function">ov</a> <a id="6786" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#6746" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a><a id="6787" class="Symbol">)}</a> <a id="6790" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="6792" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#6760" class="Bound">ğ’¦</a> <a id="6794" href="UALib.Relations.Unary.html#3001" class="Function Operator">âŠ†</a> <a id="6796" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#3950" class="Datatype">P</a><a id="6797" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="6798" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#6746" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a><a id="6799" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="6801" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#6746" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a><a id="6802" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="6804" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#6760" class="Bound">ğ’¦</a>

</pre>

We sometimes want to go back and forth between our two representations of subalgebras of algebras in a class. The tools `subalgebraâ†’S` and `Sâ†’subalgebra` are made for that purpose.

Next we observe that lifting to a higher universe does not break the property of being a subalgebra of an algebra of a class.  In other words, if we lift a subalgebra of an algebra in a class, the result is still a subalgebra of an algebra in the class.

The next lemma would be too obvoius to care about were it not for the fact that we'll need it later, so it too must be formalized.

<pre class="Agda">

#### PS(ğ’¦) âŠ† SP(ğ’¦)

Finally, we are in a position to prove that a product of subalgebras of algebras in a class ğ’¦ is a subalgebra of a product of algebras in ğ’¦.

#### <a id="products-of-classes">Products of classes</a>

Next we formally state and prove that, given an arbitrary class ğ’¦ of algebras, the product of all algebras in the class S(ğ’¦) belongs to SP(ğ’¦). That is, â¨… S(ğ’¦) âˆˆ SP(ğ’¦ ). This turns out to be a nontrivial exercise. In fact, it is not immediately obvious (at least not to this author) how one expresses the product of an entire class of algebras as a dependent type. Nonetheless, after a number of failed attempts, the right type revealed itself. (Not surprisingly, now that we have it, it seems almost obvious.)

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="17837" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="class-product"></a><a id="17844" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#17844" class="Module">class-product</a> <a id="17858" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="17859" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#17859" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a> <a id="17861" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17863" href="universes.html#551" class="Postulate">Universe</a><a id="17871" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="17873" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#17873" class="Bound">ğ’¦</a> <a id="17875" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17877" href="UALib.Relations.Unary.html#1082" class="Function">Pred</a> <a id="17882" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="17883" href="UALib.Algebras.Algebras.html#813" class="Function">Algebra</a> <a id="17891" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#17859" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a> <a id="17893" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#1882" class="Bound">ğ‘†</a><a id="17894" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="17896" href="UALib.Relations.Congruences.html#933" class="Function">ov</a> <a id="17899" href="UALib.Varieties.Varieties.html#17859" class="Bound">ğ“¤</a><a id="17900" class="Symbol">)}</a> <a id="17903" class="Keyword">where</a>

</pre>

Notice that the second component of the dependent pair is `(ğ‘¨ âˆˆ ğ’¦) Ã— (X â†’ âˆ£ ğ‘¨ âˆ£)`.  In previous versions of the [UALib][] this second component was simply `ğ‘¨ âˆˆ ğ’¦`.  However, we realized that adding a mapping of type `X â†’ âˆ£ ğ‘¨ âˆ£` is quite useful.  The reason for this will become clear later; for now, suffice it to say that a map X â†’ âˆ£ ğ‘¨ âˆ£ may be viewed as a context, and we would like to keep the context completely general.  Adding the map to the index set defined above accomplishes this.

Alternatively, we could have defined the class product in a way that explicitly displays the index, like so.

<pre class="Agda">

 <a id="19373" class="Comment">-- class-product&#39; : {ğ“¤ ğ“§ : Universe}{X : ğ“§ Ì‡} â†’ Pred (Algebra ğ“¤ ğ‘†)(ov ğ“¤) â†’ Algebra (ov ğ“¤) ğ‘†</a>
 <a id="19466" class="Comment">-- class-product&#39;{ğ“¤}{ğ“§}{X} ğ’¦ = â¨… Î» (i : (Î£ ğ‘¨ ê‰ (Algebra ğ“¤ ğ‘†) , (ğ‘¨ âˆˆ ğ’¦) Ã— (X â†’ âˆ£ ğ‘¨ âˆ£))) â†’ âˆ£ i âˆ£</a>

</pre>

If `p : ğ‘¨ âˆˆ ğ’¦` and `h : X â†’ âˆ£ ğ‘¨ âˆ£`, then we can think of the pair `(ğ‘¨ , p , h) âˆˆ â„‘ ğ’¦` as an index over the class, and so we can think of `ğ”„ (ğ‘¨ , p , h)` (which is obviously `ğ‘¨`) as the projection of the product `â¨… ( ğ”„ ğ’¦ )` onto the `(ğ‘¨ , p, h)`-th component.


#### â¨… S(ğ’¦) âˆˆ SP(ğ’¦)

Finally, we prove the result that plays an important role in the formal proof of Birkhoff's Theorem---namely, that our newly defined class product â¨… ( ğ”„ ğ’¦ ) belongs to SP(ğ’¦).

As we just saw, the (informal) product â¨… S(ğ’¦) of all subalgebras of algebras in ğ’¦ is implemented (formally) in the [UALib][] as â¨… ( ğ”„ S(ğ’¦) ), and our goal is to prove that this product belongs to SP(ğ’¦). We can do this by first proving that the product belongs to PS(ğ’¦) (in `class-prod-s-âˆˆ-ps`) and then applying the PSâŠ†SP lemma above.
